      "title": "11HRS of 4K Shark Paradise - Undersea Nature Relaxation™ Film + Music by Relax Moods",
      "description": "©https://www.NatureRelaxation.com | WATCH ON-DEMAND(No Logo/Ads) @ https://watch.naturerelaxation.com/videos/shark-paradise-4k | ABOUT: Leave your worries from the world above behind and dive into a vibrant undersea world inhabited by the iconic sharks, for 11 full hours of Nature Relaxation. Captured by filmmaker collaborator Peter Schneider, Shark Paradise features hundreds of unique real-time scenes captured from around the world, paired with gentle underwater sounds & calming music for deep relaxation by Relax Moods. MORE INFO/LINKS:\n\nABOUT SHARKS AND THEIR IMPORTANCE:\n\nSharks are a vital species for a healthy ocean, however this fact is often forgotten for dramatic impact in media publications. Understanding why their existence is crucial for our ocean cuts out any clouded judgement upon sharks that may previously exist. \n\nSharks are Apex Predators\n\nSharks are top or “apex” predators in the marine ecosystem. This is because they have very few natural predators. A cascade effect naturally occurs in a balanced, healthy ecosystem, whether it be marine or terrestrial. Sharks as the apex predator, act as a regulator for biodiversity. They directly limit the abundance of species below them in the cascade or food chain. Sharks diets are especially varied, so that no one species of prey will become low in numbers through over predation. If certain populations of prey are low, sharks are able to switch to another food source. This continues throughout the food chain, and is a sign of a healthy, biodiverse ecosystem. It is a naturally occurring event, which is greatly important, to provide a balance of species within the ecosystem itself. \n\nAn Ocean Without Sharks \n\nStudies have shown that the greater abundance of sharks, the greater the diversity of species. When comparing two reefs, one with sharks and one without, the latter circumstance showed species absences. Without sharks, there is a risk of over predation by the middle to lower predatory species with evidence of over eating of vegetation or primary producers (kelp, phytoplankton, or sea grass). Herbivorous preying species are in abundance with increased competition on food sources, called a “Top-Down” effect. This results in surplus of middle predatory species, and overeating of the lowest species on the food chain which ultimately effects the species richness, and biodiversity upon the reef. If this was to occur on a larger scale, it could be catastrophic. The health of the ocean would decline, and seriously affect the way we live. \n\nSharks have been on this planet for 450 million years, and are amazing creatures. They come in many different types, from the gentle Whale shark, to the notorious Great White. Sharks are important for our ocean’s survival and need to be protected. There should be more concern of an ocean without sharks, rather than a beach with sightings and baited drum lines. As the apex predators of our largest ecosystem, sharks deserve our respect and our conservation efforts to protect them. \n\nWe hope this video helps raise the appreciation and love for the amazing sharks of the world! Officially the Hanwha 63 City, it's a skyscraper on Yeouido island, overlooking the Han River in Seoul, South Korea. It was designed by the American architectural firm Skidmore, Owings & Merrill. At 250 meters (819 ft) high, it was the tallest building outside North America when it opened in July 1985. The 63 Building was built as a landmark for the 1988 Summer Olympics.\n\nNamsan tower is a communication and observation tower located on Namsan Mountain in central Seoul, South Korea, and is the highest point in Seoul.
